[17-May-19 06:47 AM] Audo#5667
Hello everyone,

I have been part of this community for a long time but never really introduced myself.

Currently, I am travelling a lot, like a digital nomad style. If there are Komodo events & meetups let me know and maybe I'll come üòÉ The reason why I like this project & community is its open source nature and strong values on decentralization and working technology. That's why I joined back in the day, and that's why I am still here.

Apart from being part of the Komodo marketing team, I am also involved in 'Komodo Pioneers' project. We just got the great news today that we were officially elected to run a second notary node. Our mission is to use some of the funds we generate to support the Komodo community. Mostly we have done this through meetups but we are open for ideas.

If you would like to help the Komodo ecosystem someway shoot me a message and we will see if we can help. Be aware that Pioneers is only giving out micro-funding and prefers to build relationships versus one-time advertising.

[19-May-19 03:02 PM] Regnar#6164
Hi all!
I'm Regnar, I've been hanging around Komodo since the BTCD > KMD swap days. I was never really a programmer but the longer I've hung around here the more I've started to learn and so I've started actively teaching myself. You can usually find me around random projects helping in anyway I can, always on a volunteer basis, as I do work full time outside of crypto. 

A little while back I had the honor of having my name put up on the Komodo team page as a key community contributor and I'm also community support in a few different Komodo ecosystem projects here in Discord. If you have any questions or just want to say Hi don't be shy or afraid to reach out!

[19-Feb-20 09:59 PM] Audo#5667
hey @theblockstalk , I am interested to hear your thoughts and comparisons. I don't know much about what's happening in the eosio ecosystem or what kind of similarities we might have. 

It's great to get fresh eyes on Komodo


[20-Feb-20 11:18 AM] theblockstalk#6501
AFAIK and as i think are important...

Similarities:
- multi-chain autonomous customizable blockchain ecosystem
- public / private blockchains
- free txs possible

Komodo
1. consensus is configutable when chain launches to POW, POS and POA (permissions)
2. consensus configuration can be upgraded with a hard fork
3. UTXO model
4. Bitcoin script "contracts"
5. Contact upgrading not possible after deployed
6. All txs are free???
7. BaaS to start Smart Chains easily
8. lots of pre built official standardized dApps (channels, DEXs etc)
9. private contacts are optional and standardized
10. 1000 tps
11. Interoperability solution built in with merkle roots on all chains
12. 10s block time???
13. ...

Eosio
1. consensus POS, dPOS, POA or anything that can be programmed in a smart contact
2. consensus can be changed through soft fork (upgrading the system contracts in consensus). Hard forks have standardized upgrade patterns to increase transparency during upgrades)
3. account model
4. Wasm contracts programmed in C++
5. contact upgradability by default (including system/governance contracts)
6. tx billing can be customized per chain, and also per smart contact
7. ...
8. ...
9. Private contacts possible but not standardized or built in
10. 10,000 - 25,000 tps (have not verified recently but believe this is the range for eosio V2)
11. Interoperability possible but not built
12. 0.5s block time
13. Contract argument types (e.g. strings, integers) are not serialised/parsed before entering a contract - block explorers / signature providers can easily show users the readable  data that is being signed instead of hex strings


[20-Feb-20 11:36 AM] theblockstalk#6501
lastly, EOS and eosio are confused by anyone out of the ecostem which is creating a reputation and education problem for other chains using eosio...


[20-Feb-20 07:04 PM] gcharang#6833
some corrections:
> 4. Bitcoin script "contracts"
not really. they extend the bitcoin script with operations that are more than 1000x complex. ex: all the Antara modules are represented on the blockchain similar to bitcoin script(OP codes and hexes) but the functionality they provide is programmed using C/C++ 
> 10. 1000 tps
that is per chain. Komodo smart chains can have parallel chains launched to increase scalability. Ex: A chain named SCALER has hit its tx limit. to accommodate more tps, a new chain SCALER1 can be launched. its coin is the same as the coin present on the SCALER chain without affecting the total supply 
> 12. 10s block time
is the recommeded minimum for public networks. going below that could make achieving consensus difficult
> 6. free transactions?
all transactions are cheap. not free. the standard is 0.0001 COIN
>  5. contract upgrading after deployed
can be done with a hardfork and sometimes a softfork


[20-Feb-20 11:38 PM] theblockstalk#6501

[12-Jun-20 07:11 AM] xxxencryptacion#3788
Question - is there default solidity type language for creating smart contacts via Antara Modules


[12-Jun-20 07:11 AM] xxxencryptacion#3788
For KMD smart chains ... thank you!


[12-Jun-20 07:17 AM] gcharang#6833
@xxxencryptacion Antara modules are different from ETH smart contracts. the main difference is that, a smart chain will only run trusted "contracts", the "contract" code is in the daemon and not in the blockchain. as such, all the existing Antara modules are written in C/CPP. but, tools to write them in py,rust are in dev/testing

you might find this discussion useful:
https://discord.com/channels/412898016371015680/428673045767520260/719018957008404611


[12-Jun-20 07:48 AM] xxxencryptacion#3788
Yes we are building a synthetic trading platform of our native token - like currency futures ....


[12-Jun-20 07:49 AM] xxxencryptacion#3788
we've done decent amount of reading on KMD, launching a native token, user end points etc. But would actually like to program our franchise via turing complete language


[12-Jun-20 07:51 AM] xxxencryptacion#3788
We would essentially have a smart contract for each of the top 50 cryptocurrencies, and would need to code (1) duration of the contract, (2) futures price and (3) valuation multiple - these are notional instruments, kind of like sports fantasy betting draftkings.com


[12-Jun-20 07:53 AM] xxxencryptacion#3788
P&L would be settled then in our native token üòÑ


[12-Jun-20 07:54 AM] xxxencryptacion#3788
We have other high finance applications in development too for what KMD might be more suited in the immediate term, but figured to ask about SC, our other platform alternative is TRX


[12-Jun-20 07:57 AM] xxxencryptacion#3788
Yes thanks for the reference, been doing a decent amount of reading and are aware of ETH shortcomings and the expensive VM they are running, do not like it one bit LOL

[12-Dec-20 02:01 PM] KMD TipBot#0077

{Embed}
TipBot Help
`!kmdtip`
Displays this message
`!kmdtip info`
Displays coin information
`!kmdtip balance`
Displays your balance
`!kmdtip deposit`
Displays your deposit address
`!kmdtip withdraw <address> <amount|all>`
Withdraws the entered amount to a KMD address of your choice, e.g.
`!kmdtip withdraw GLM3n7yMFmYkas2AgHKqE6EMJW5VsUXtQn 5.20`
*Note: Minimal amount to withdraw: 0.1 KMD. A withdrawal fee of 0.02 KMD will be automatically deducted from the amount.* *Additionally, 10% of deducted withdrawal fee will be donated to the bot author to help continual development.*
`!kmdtip <@user> <amount|all> [private]`
Tips the @ mentioned user with the desired amount, e.g.
`!kmdtip @test123456#7890 1.00`
`!kmdtip rain <amount|all> [<@role>]`
Rains the desired amount onto all online users  (optionally, within specified role), e.g.
`!kmdtip rain 10.00`, `!kmdtip rain 10.00 @Supporters`
`!kmdtip soak <amount|all> [<@role>]`
Soaks the desired amount onto all online and idle users (optionally, within specified role), e.g.
`!kmdtip soak 5.00`, `!kmdtip soak 5.00 @Supporters`
`!kmdtip flood <amount|all> [<@role>]`
Floods the desired amount onto all users (*including offline users*) (optionally, within specified role), e.g.
`!kmdtip flood 5.00`, `!kmdtip flood 5.00 @Supporters`
`!kmdtip thunder <amount|all> [<@role>]`
Tips a random lucky online user with the amount (optionally, within specified role), e.g.
`!kmdtip thunder 5.00`, `!kmdtip thunder 5.00 @Supporters`
`!kmdtip thunderstorm <numberOfUsers> <amount|all> [<@role>]`
Tips a specified number (max: 50) random lucky online users with part of the amount (optionally, within specified role), e.g.
`!kmdtip thunderstorm 10 5.00`, `!kmdtip thunderstorm 10 5.00 @Supporters`
`!kmdtip hurricane <numberOfUsers> <amount|all> [<@role>]`
Tips a specified number (max: 50) random lucky online and idle users with part of the amount (optionally, within specified role), e.g.
`!kmdtip hurricane 10 5.00`, `!kmdtip hurricane 10 5.00 @Supporters`
`!kmdtip faucet`
Gets an amount from the faucet (applicable every 4 hours)
`!kmdtip listtransactions <numberOfDays>`
Generates an audit log of user's transactions for the last specified number of days
`!kmdtip blockheight`
Gets the current block height and block hash
`!kmdtip peers`
Generates an `addnode` list
Sapphire TipBot by sclear#0274
